<div id="review_2704197201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2704197201" />
    <a title="Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7287572-grace"><img alt="Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598731006p2/7287572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2704197201?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/7287572-grace">Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780152064013" href="/book/show/3312154-dragon-s-keep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7287572-grace?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7287572-grace?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7287572-grace?shelf=very-much-yes">very-much-yes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2704197201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10034307599152893337">The summary of this book lets you know two things: that Rosie is born with a dragon claw on her hand, and that eventually she is carried off by a dragon. <br/><br/>Given this, I expected her to be carried off quite soon, but in reality more than half the book passes before she is finally princess-napped. The pace of <i>Dragon's Keep</i> is incremental, passing through two years incident by seemingly-unrelated incident, until everything changes. This book is hardcore, not shying away from murder or torture or the</span>
  <span id="freeText10034307599152893337" style="display:none">The summary of this book lets you know two things: that Rosie is born with a dragon claw on her hand, and that eventually she is carried off by a dragon. <br /><br />Given this, I expected her to be carried off quite soon, but in reality more than half the book passes before she is finally princess-napped. The pace of <i>Dragon's Keep</i> is incremental, passing through two years incident by seemingly-unrelated incident, until everything changes. This book is hardcore, not shying away from murder or torture or the awful realization that the ones you love are not good people. Sensory details are described, realistic to a point that might be uncomfortable. <br /><br />The first part of the book was good, but the best part comes obviously when she lives with the dragons. I love the dragon family and the uneasy dynamic between them and Rosie, being a slave to them and yet not being able to help caring about them. The ending wasn't <i>quite</i> what I wished it was, but given that imperfection is a huge theme of the book, I'll accept it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10034307599152893337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5006378294732086113">Not my favorite book. I read it for a challenge. I found the dragon claw story to be interesting and confusing at the same time. I liked that the dragon took her away and that he recognized her beauty and accepted her for who she was. I hated all the deaths in this book, but there was a certain beauty to the story. I would recommend this book to anyone who likes dragons and fantasy, and romance.</span>

<div id="review_1538798007" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1538798007" />
    <a title="Courtney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1739351-courtney"><img alt="Courtney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343846657p2/1739351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1538798007?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney" href="/user/show/1739351-courtney">Courtney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=teen-fiction">teen-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1538798007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1008894686108619107">A very, very long time ago, Merlin made a prophecy about a future princess of Wilde Island. It would take roughly 600 years to come true, but this future heir would put an end to a deadly war and restore honor to the Pendragon name. <br/>Princess Rosalind knows that she is the princess mentioned in the prophecy; her mother has made every decision with this prophecy in mind. All in all, Rosalind is a fairly typical princess - she is fair and pretty, well-educated and well-mannered. All that's left is </span>
  <span id="freeText1008894686108619107" style="display:none">A very, very long time ago, Merlin made a prophecy about a future princess of Wilde Island. It would take roughly 600 years to come true, but this future heir would put an end to a deadly war and restore honor to the Pendragon name. <br />Princess Rosalind knows that she is the princess mentioned in the prophecy; her mother has made every decision with this prophecy in mind. All in all, Rosalind is a fairly typical princess - she is fair and pretty, well-educated and well-mannered. All that's left is to find her a prince. Although there is one detail that threatens to ruin everything: Rosalind was born with a dragon's talon in place of her left ring finger. To hide this, the queen and Rosalind always wear golden gloves whenever they might be seen. Attempts have been made to remedy the situation, all to no avail. <br />In the meantime, dragon attacks have been getting worse and worse. When a visiting royal entourage slays one of the dragons that's been terrorizing the village, a massive celebration is ordered. The celebration turns out to be ill-conceived. Rosalind is kidnapped by the dead dragon's mate and flown off to his lair along with a handful of dragon eggs ripped from the dead dragon. Instead of eating Rosalind, the dragon - Lord Faul, puts her to work preparing for hatching some baby dragons. Rosalind finds no kindness in her new surroundings, but she does find a sense of peace. No longer must she hide her talon (the dragons think it's the only part of her that isn't disgusting); no longer must she worry about her role in 600-year-old prophecies. As a bonus, she has a deal with Lord Faul and his offspring that she will not speak to any humans if they don't eat any humans. Relative peace at last. For a while, anyway.<br />This unusual medieval fantasy gives readers an up-close and personal view of living with dragons. In this world, dragons are nearly extinct and are generally viewed by humans as deadly monsters. As Rosalind finds, while dragons are indeed dangerous, they are not irrational and are capable of love and compassion. Rosalind herself grows significantly as a character. Her life as a princess was marked by arrogance and royal superiority, all of which is brusquely stripped away when she is kidnapped. <u>Dragon's Keep</u> doesn't always feel like a typical fantasy novel, which is not to say that it doesn't have a few fantastical conceits. Readers should be prepared for an excessively high body count (particularly in a book geared towards a younger audience). Questions about the motivations of characters will leave readers with much to ponder, while under-developed romance and the occasional slow pacing at times might leave other readers wondering why they should bother. There's both a lot to like and to dislike in this novel; I'm personally on the fence. My middle school book group seemed to enjoy it, though they certainly had their issues with it as well. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1008894686108619107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1093922057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1093922057" />
    <a title="Aelvana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33911745-aelvana"><img alt="Aelvana" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1093922057?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aelvana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aelvana" href="/user/show/33911745-aelvana">Aelvana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1093922057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17459101803728073128">Rosaline was born with a dragon's claw on her left hand in place of her ring finger. All her life she's worn gloves to keep it hidden. Despite Rosaline's deformity, her mother is convinced she's the one who will fulfill Merlin's prophecy of peace and restoration. But not all the healers in the kingdom can help against this ailment, especially when Rosaline can't tell them what it is. Then the dragons come, and Rosaline goes from pampered princess to dragon servant. The dragons see her claw as th</span>
  <span id="freeText17459101803728073128" style="display:none">Rosaline was born with a dragon's claw on her left hand in place of her ring finger. All her life she's worn gloves to keep it hidden. Despite Rosaline's deformity, her mother is convinced she's the one who will fulfill Merlin's prophecy of peace and restoration. But not all the healers in the kingdom can help against this ailment, especially when Rosaline can't tell them what it is. Then the dragons come, and Rosaline goes from pampered princess to dragon servant. The dragons see her claw as the only part of her that isn't deformed. Rosaline longs to escape, but her promise binds her. When she does return, she finally understands the meaning of the prophecy spoken over her long before her birth even as she brings it to completion.<br /><br />This is, essentially, a retelling of the fairy tale of a queen who could have no children and went to a witch for a potion which turned out to have its origins in dragons. I need to look back for the title of that other book, because I liked that one much better than this. (Found it: the story in question was actually a short story in Bruce Coville's Half Human anthology, the story titled Princess Dragonblood, by Jude Mandell)<br /><br />As with all books based on a prophecy, particularly one from Merlin, whom we are assured is never wrong, the plot has to work hard to remain interesting despite completely giving away the ending. I'm not sure it works. At least for me, because I am familiar with that myth, the book simply read like a longer version of it. I would also have liked it much, much better if Merlin hadn't been the one to make the prophecy, if the Pendragons hadn't been mentioned, and so on. Merlin, Arthur, and all the rest only serve as the very briefest backdrop. Why not make the seer someone with less connotations, since the relevance of the Arthurian legend is never explained?<br /><br />On more of a positive note, the book was very true to the customs of the time in which it was set. The witch hunts, the local superstitions, and the trial all remained very much in period. The fact that all three give the average person less intelligence than a sheep is somewhat unfortunate.<br /><br />I can't say I disliked the book, since it was engaging enough, but I can't say I really liked it either. The story added nothing to what I originally knew of the myth, and honestly I liked the way the short story portrayed it better. And I wanted to strangle just about every person living in that town for being such gullible idiots. Neutral.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17459101803728073128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Cory Dorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25121808-cory-dorn"><img alt="Cory Dorn" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cory Dorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cory Dorn" href="/user/show/25121808-cory-dorn">Cory Dorn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1051170671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3580072098333340970">I enjoyed this book because it starts in a place I have always wanted to visit, which is Europe. In this book it starts on Wilde island, which is in Europe somewhere. The time was 1145 A.D. The story begins 600's year ago when Merlin writes a prophecy of a princess name Rosalind. The story is told in first person point of view by Rosalind. Rosalind has a lot of ups and downs through out this whole book, because of the curse that she tries to hide. Rosalind's curse is she has one dragon claw as a</span>
  <span id="freeText3580072098333340970" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book because it starts in a place I have always wanted to visit, which is Europe. In this book it starts on Wilde island, which is in Europe somewhere. The time was 1145 A.D. The story begins 600's year ago when Merlin writes a prophecy of a princess name Rosalind. The story is told in first person point of view by Rosalind. Rosalind has a lot of ups and downs through out this whole book, because of the curse that she tries to hide. Rosalind's curse is she has one dragon claw as a finger. Rosalind is very likable, because she is a really nice person. You see her being nice throughout the whole book. For example when she goes to live with the dragon, she takes care of his pips. Kye one of allied knights of Rosalinds kingdom, kills the dragon's wife. Later in the book she makes a deal with the dragon if he stops killing her rescuers or killing anymore humans, she will stay with the pips until they are grown. Which I do not understand why the dragon keeps that promise. Rosalind's mother killed one of the dragons baby, which would be the dragon pips older sister. The reason why Rosalind's mother did this is to have a baby. The dragon egg yolk created an egg in her belly to make the queen be able to have Rosalind. This is what creates Rosalind's curse to have the dragon claw.<br /> <br />The characters in this book are Rosalind, she tries to make peace with the dragon and get him to stop killing and in return she will care for its pips. Rosalind's mother also plays a role because of her Rosalind is cursed by the mother drinking the yolk from a dragon egg. <br /><br />The setting starts off in 1145 A.D, or the medieval times, on Wilde Island, Europe. The setting is really important to this book because they have a lot of medieval references during the medieval times in Europe. For example queens, kings, knights, sirs, and dragons are all talked about in other medieval books.<br /><br />I recommended this to teenagers that are between the ages of 12-16. I say this because teens today are afraid to show their true self, and it shows that even if you are hideous there is always somebody who will love you.</span>

<div id="review_1085134275" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1085134275" />
    <a title="Tamara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/862583-tamara"><img alt="Tamara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401981536p2/862583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1085134275?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tamara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tamara" href="/user/show/862583-tamara">Tamara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/862583-tamara?shelf=hard-copy">hard-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/862583-tamara?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/862583-tamara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/862583-tamara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/862583-tamara?shelf=has-a-love-story">has-a-love-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/862583-tamara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085134275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13008763111496985094">This book is quite different from what I expected going into it, but that ended up being okay when I finally let go of those expectations. It did make me want to re-read the second book (which I read several years ago without realizing there was a first book), though, so that’s what I’m going to do.<br/><br/>I had a difficult time liking Rosalind’s mother. Scratch that, I didn’t really like her at all. I understand doing anything you can to protect your child, but I felt more like the Queen was trying to </span>
  <span id="freeText13008763111496985094" style="display:none">This book is quite different from what I expected going into it, but that ended up being okay when I finally let go of those expectations. It did make me want to re-read the second book (which I read several years ago without realizing there was a first book), though, so that’s what I’m going to do.<br /><br />I had a difficult time liking Rosalind’s mother. Scratch that, I didn’t really like her at all. I understand doing anything you can to protect your child, but I felt more like the Queen was trying to protect her idea of Rosalind as the 21st queen rather than protect Rosalind herself. Although Rose didn’t start out as a bad person, she was rather spoiled and sheltered; however, I liked her more as the book progressed. In addition to maturing, she also developed other important traits, such as hard work and compassion, as well as learning to let go of prejudices she had been taught.<br /><br />The dragons’ words and actions were very humanlike, and sometimes it was difficult to imagine them doing the things they were described as doing (like using a broom—how?). But they had their own unique personalities (dragonalities?), and I liked seeing their growth, as well.<br /><br />As I mentioned before, I had previously read the second book, <i>Dragonswood</i>, and had wondered why certain characters had dragon parts, like Rosalind in this book. I appreciated finding out how that happened, as Rosalind was the first.<br /><br />I wasn’t at all expecting a bunch of witch hunt stuff, but I suppose I shouldn’t have been surprised. I think my biggest complaint was how abrupt the ending was. I would have liked it to be a little longer, especially since—let’s be honest—the time given to building up the Rosalind’s romantic relationship is negligible. It’s more of a brief hint partway though the book of what could be, and then nothing after that until what is essentially a brief epilogue. After the experiences in the last few chapters, I think it needed more than a rapid ending to wrap it up.<br /><br />How it ends: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[After trying unsuccessfully to get pregnant for six years, Rosalind’s mother had gone to Demetra (a witch?) for help. She gave the queen slime from a dragon egg to drink, and the queen was able to get pregnant; however, Rosalind was born with a dragon claw instead of her left ring finger and was forced to always wear gloves to hide it from everyone but her own mother. (The Queen had also set in place a second plan: Her lady’s maid, Alissandra, got pregnant and hid away. The Queen would use pillows to feign pregnancy until Aliss gave birth, and then the baby would be passed as the Queen’s. Since she got pregnant, she made Aliss stay with Demetra. She and her daughter, Kit, became Demetra’s servants.) Anyone who may have seen Rose’s talon mysteriously died (it ended up being the Queen).<br /><br />After every healer they summoned (without explaining what was wrong) failed to cure Rose, the Queen took her to Demetra to try to remove her claw, but the treatments made it bigger. When they left, Rose took Kit with her to be her lady's maid. The Queen allowed it because Kit was mute.<br /><br />A group of knights comes from Empress Matilda to see Rosalind and to make arrangements for reinforcements from Wilde Island in the war against King Stephan. Rose begins to develop feelings for Kye, Lord Godrick's son, and it appears it might be mutual. But it's really on the beginning of things--a crush, basically (this was one of my complaints). The men (mainly Kye, who was defending his father) kill the female dragon, and the people celebrate and are very disrespectful towards the body, which bothers both Kye and Rose. The dragon's mate comes and sort of attacks as he mourns, but his main goal is to retrieve the eggs that his lady were carrying. He says four, but one falls into the ocean. Later, Kye takes Rose to a cave to see a dragon egg shell that he found; they both admire it, though I think they're each afraid of what the other thinks.<br /><br />Rose attends a hunt with her father and the Empress's men. Rose's horse falls down a ravine, her ankle breaks, and she is attacked by wolves. Kye saves her and pulls her gloves off while trying to attend to her wounds. He sees the talon and doesn't speak again, though he carries her up to her father. While she is in bed healing, Lord Godrick and his men leave, and so does Rose's father and his men.<br /><br />Rose's mother finally gets her out for May Day, and that's when Rose is taken by the dragon, whose name is Lord Faul. She is forced to basically be a servant and helps him prepare for the hatching of the eggs. She has to gather milkweed and thistle to make bitter milk for them to drink, as well as clean up after them. She ends up learning the dragons' language.<br /><br />Niles Broderick and others try to save Rose, but they are all killed except for Niles. Rose makes a deal with Lord Faul: she will stay with the dragons and never speak to another human as long as he spares Niles and stops eating people. As part of the deal, they fly back to the castle, and Rose tosses her gloves at her mother.<br /><br />Over time, she develops a sort of connection with the dragons. They all admire her dragon claw and view it as a part of the older sister they would have had if Demetra hadn't stolen an egg. Kit shows up during a bad storm to try to convince Rose to go home--the king and queen are both dead, her mother is in the dungeon, and Sir Magnus is trying to become king. They are unable to save Kadmi, one of the boy dragons, when he is trapped under a fallen tree. Ore is swept away, and Kit goes after her. Kit was able to save Ore, but she died in the process. Lord Faul dies from grief, despite everything Rose and the other dragons do to keep him alive.<br /><br />The three remaining dragons return Rose to her kingdom, telling her to take her throne before they fly away to find the other dragons their father told them about. Rose is accused of being a witch and is kept in the dungeon before undergoing a trial, presided over by Magnus, at which many people unexpectedly accuse her of various witchy deeds. She is forced to walk over coals. When her feet haven't healed in three days, she is about to be hanged. She tries to escape and is grabbed by a Benedictine monk, who turns out to be Kye. He says he has proof of her blood and starts speaking to the people before pulling out Evaine's scepter, which he had found at Dragon's Keep when he went searching for Rose (she thought he was going to show everyone her talon). He tells the people to honor their queen, who has given up so much for them to be safe.<br /><br />Rosalind and Kye are wed and rule together as king and queen. The three dragons return with four others. Eetha pulls off Rose's gloves, and she, Ore, and Chawl all kiss her talon as the people watch (they end up thinking the dragon's gave her the talon then). Kye breaks his sword and lays it at the dragons' feet. So the prophecy about the dragon's giving a talon and the king laying his sword at their feet comes to pass, thus ending the war between the people of Wilde Island and the dragons. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Note: There may have been some mild swearing, but I can't remember it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13008763111496985094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_347596163" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/347596163" />
    <a title="Lianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2517297-lianne"><img alt="Lianne" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/347596163?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lianne" href="/user/show/2517297-lianne">Lianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517297-lianne?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517297-lianne?shelf=best-bets-for-girls">best-bets-for-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517297-lianne?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer347596163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6082563604365450177">Since it's been a while (published 2007), I decided to reread this before I read Dragonswood. This book was just as wonderful the second time and the cover is still one of the best ever. Far superior to the one on Dragonswood. I don't like the current trend in cover design. They are all starting to look the same.<br/><br/>Although I love the phenomenon of books published by young authors, when I read this book, I am reminded of the fullness and depth of a story told by an accomplished and confident author</span>
  <span id="freeText6082563604365450177" style="display:none">Since it's been a while (published 2007), I decided to reread this before I read Dragonswood. This book was just as wonderful the second time and the cover is still one of the best ever. Far superior to the one on Dragonswood. I don't like the current trend in cover design. They are all starting to look the same.<br /><br />Although I love the phenomenon of books published by young authors, when I read this book, I am reminded of the fullness and depth of a story told by an accomplished and confident author. Yes, for every young Sherwood Smith, Amelia Atwater-Rhodes, or S. E. Hinton, there is a Christopher Paolini who's promise is enticing but ultimately disappointing.<br /><br />Dragon's Keep is a unique blending of history and fantasy. Carey imagines an island near England six hundred years after the story of Merlin and King Arthur, where Arthur's sister's descendents have ruled.<br /><br />Wilde Island used to be home to dragons and fey. Although the people live in fear of a predatory dragon, humans have overrun the island until the fey and other magical creatures have disappeared.<br /><br />Princess Rosalind, the royal heir, was born with a terrible secret. She knows that her disfigurement makes her unfit to rule; unfit to be loved. With her mother's help, she hides it from everyone. Her mother, convinced that her daughter has a unique destiny to fulfill, will stop at nothing to keep their secret.<br /><br />There are so many surprises and plot twists here, from Merlin's prophecies regarding the destiny of the twenty-first ruler of Wilde Island to dragon attacks to murder. But the real story is the kindness, bravery, and perseverance of Princess Rosalind, a princess who, because Carey is such a confident and accomplished storyteller, is a fully realized young woman whose inner beauty shines brightly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6082563604365450177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('J8ZHSZJtfpnIECjD8qfR+AMWgiYbFChw915EzqmYQy7q5P2X2ePK72id5SGutOFPpZZ247uwtJ+duNSnHTFZpA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6eWu964TnkVvtYyKAIYsulYv0C1MGuXJ4CVwkH8S7h8kxxQp5Z0qM884QWhclRwN8K8k6Oy+eSaKw+D5y7v0lQ==')})
  }
